%%***>>>text element-link:[[Fourier Series Convergence]]<<<***%%Fourier Series Convergence ^vxXRvDz6

in order to converge f and f' ^bHqFmXD6

must be piecewise continuous and have a finite # of
discontinuities at a finite # of points. Fourier Series
converge to average of f at a discontinuity point ^Z34YeCr7

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Fourier Series - Periodic Extension]]<<<***%%FS - Periodic Extension ^XQNY8cnr

2p is the fundamental period of ^vkvSMBJa

the sum. Periodic Extension two ways: 1. Non-periodic f(x)
solve fs over some interval. resulting fs will represent 
different function that matches f over period and then
repeats. 2. periodic f(x). can automatically represent
f(x) over all x by solving fs over single period ^pV5G7WuO

%%***>>>text element-link:[[FS - Partial Sum]]<<<***%%FS - Partial Sum ^wr3ml76R

the first n terms of the fourier series ^wCriWpM2

as n increases accuracy becomes better (closer to f(x)) ^mYZL67ir

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Fourier Series - Even_Odd Functions]]<<<***%%FS - Even-Odd Functions ^FrTG3GRT

if f(x) = odd (f(-x) = -f(x)). The fs of f 
is entirely sine terms (an = 0, a0 = 0) 
if f(x) = even (f(-x) = f(x)). The fs 
of f is entirely cos terms (bn = 0) ^T8UDOa8o

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Fourier Series - Half-Range Expansion]]<<<***%%FS - Half-Range Expansion ^tsV2Amgw

to create a useable expansion of f over (0,L). 3 ways: ^HTE3ynES

1. f from (-L to L)(p=L) such that f is even (bn = 0)
2. f from (-L to L)(p=L) such that f is odd (an/0=0)
3. f from (0 to L)(a to a+2p)(2p=L) ^f5j7UO4r

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Complex Fourier Series]]<<<***%%Complex Fourier Series ^JiZaPueV

 ^NaJJvEaa

semi-infinite interval
even/odd rules apply ^MtYqgLeA
